				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=PepsiCo_Inc.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="PepsiCo Inc.">PepsiCo Inc.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the company. For the soft drink, see <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<p><b>PepsiCo, Inc.</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> food, snack, and <a href="/wiki/Beverage_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverage corporation">beverage corporation</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Harrison,_New_York" title="Harrison, New York">Harrison, New York</a>, in the hamlet of <a href="/wiki/Purchase,_New_York" title="Purchase, New York">Purchase</a>. PepsiCo has interests in the manufacturing, marketing, and distribution of grain-based snack foods, beverages, and other products. PepsiCo was formed in 1965 with the merger of the <b>Pepsi-Cola Company</b> and <a href="/wiki/Frito-Lay" title="Frito-Lay">Frito-Lay</a>, Inc. PepsiCo has since expanded from its namesake product <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> to a broader range of food and beverage brands, the largest of which included an acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Products" title="Tropicana Products">Tropicana Products</a> in 1998 and the <a href="/wiki/Quaker_Oats_Company" title="Quaker Oats Company">Quaker Oats Company</a> in 2001, which added the <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a> brand to its portfolio.

Wikidata" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/10px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png" decoding="async" width="10" height="10" style="vertical-align: text-top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/15px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/20px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>As of January 26, 2012, 22 of PepsiCo's brands generated retail sales of more than $1 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-billions_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billions-3">[3]</a></sup> and the company's products were distributed across more than 200 countries, resulting in annual <a href="/wiki/Net_revenue" class="mw-redirect" title="Net revenue">net revenues</a> of $43.3 billion. Based on net revenue, PepsiCo is the second largest food and beverage business in the world, behind <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a>. Within North America, PepsiCo is the largest food and beverage business by net revenue. <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Laguarta" title="Ramon Laguarta">Ramon Laguarta</a> has been the chief executive of PepsiCo since 2018. The company's beverage distribution and bottling is conducted by PepsiCo as well as by licensed bottlers in certain regions.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PepsiCo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PepsiCo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The soft drink Pepsi was developed by <a href="/wiki/Caleb_Bradham" title="Caleb Bradham">Caleb Bradham</a>, a pharmacist and businessman from <a href="/wiki/Duplin_County,_North_Carolina" title="Duplin County, North Carolina">Duplin County, North Carolina</a>. He coined the name "Pepsi-Cola" in 1898 while marketing the drink from his pharmacy in <a href="/wiki/New_Bern,_North_Carolina" title="New Bern, North Carolina">New Bern, North Carolina</a>. As his drink gained popularity, Bradham founded the Pepsi-Cola Company in 1902 and registered a patent for his recipe in 1903.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The company was incorporated in Delaware in 1919. Bradham's company experienced years of success leading up <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. However, sugar rationing during the war and a volatile sugar market in the war's aftermath damaged the company's financial health to such a degree that in 1923, Bradham declared <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankruptcy</a> and returned to running pharmacies in North Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p><p>On June 8, 1923 the company trademark and secret recipe were purchased by Craven Holding Corporation. In 1931, Roy Megargel, a Wall Street broker, purchased the Pepsi trademark, business, and goodwill from Craven Holding in association with <a href="/wiki/Charles_Guth" title="Charles Guth">Charles Guth</a>. Guth was also the president of <a href="/wiki/Loft,_Incorporated" class="mw-redirect" title="Loft, Incorporated">Loft, Incorporated</a>, a leading candy manufacturer based in Long Island City, New York. Loft ran a network with 115 stores across the Mid Atlantic at the time of Guth's acquisition. Guth used Loft's labs and chemists to reformulate the Pepsi syrup recipe, and he used his position as president of the company to replace <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> with Pepsi Cola at Loft's shops and restaurants. Guth also used Loft resources to promote Pepsi, and moved the soda company to a location close by Loft's own facilities in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p><p>In 1935, the shareholders of Loft sued Guth for his 91% stake of Pepsi-Cola Company in the landmark case <i><a href="/wiki/Guth_v._Loft_Inc." title="Guth v. Loft Inc.">Guth v. Loft Inc.</a></i> Loft won the suit and on May 29, 1941 formally absorbed Pepsi into Loft, which was then re-branded as Pepsi-Cola Company that same year. Loft restaurants and candy stores were spun off at this time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In the early 1960s, Pepsi-Cola's product lines expanded with the creation of <a href="/wiki/Diet_Pepsi" title="Diet Pepsi">Diet Pepsi</a> and purchase of <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Dew" title="Mountain Dew">Mountain Dew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fundhist_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fundhist-7">[7]</a></sup> In 1965, the Pepsi-Cola Company merged with Frito-Lay, Inc. to become PepsiCo, Inc. At the time of its foundation, PepsiCo was incorporated in the state of <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> and headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, New York. The company's headquarters were relocated to the present location of <a href="/wiki/Purchase,_New_York" title="Purchase, New York">Purchase, New York</a> in 1970,<sup id="cite_ref-hqmoved_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hqmoved-8">[8]</a></sup> and in 1986 PepsiCo was reincorporated in the state of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-incorp_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incorp-9">[9]</a></sup> After 39 years trading on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>, PepsiCo moved its shares to <a href="/wiki/Nasdaq" title="Nasdaq">Nasdaq</a> on December 20, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions_and_divestments">Acquisitions and divestments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PepsiCo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Acquisitions and divestments" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Between the late-1970s and the mid-1990s, PepsiCo expanded via acquisition of businesses outside of its core focus of packaged food and beverage brands; however it exited these non-core business lines largely in 1997, selling some, and spinning off others into a new company named <a href="/wiki/Tricon_Global_Restaurants" class="mw-redirect" title="Tricon Global Restaurants">Tricon Global Restaurants</a>, which later became known as <a href="/wiki/Yum!_Brands" title="Yum! Brands">Yum! Brands, Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-yumhist_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yumhist-11">[11]</a></sup> PepsiCo also previously owned several other brands that it later sold so it could focus on its primary snack food and beverage lines, according to investment analysts reporting on the divestments in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-spinoff_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spinoff-12">[12]</a></sup> Brands formerly owned by PepsiCo include: <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-triconspinoff_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triconspinoff-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taco_Bell" title="Taco Bell">Taco Bell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-triconspinoff_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triconspinoff-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-triconspinoff_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triconspinoff-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hot_%27n_Now" title="Hot 'n Now">Hot 'n Now</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-hotnnow_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hotnnow-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/East_Side_Mario%27s" title="East Side Mario's">East Side Mario's</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-eastsidemarios_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eastsidemarios-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/D%27Angelo_Sandwich_Shops" class="mw-redirect" title="D'Angelo Sandwich Shops">D'Angelo Sandwich Shops</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-dangelo_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dangelo-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chevys_Fresh_Mex" title="Chevys Fresh Mex">Chevys Fresh Mex</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_Pizza_Kitchen" title="California Pizza Kitchen">California Pizza Kitchen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-calpizza_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-calpizza-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stolichnaya" title="Stolichnaya">Stolichnaya</a><sup id="cite_ref-pepsirussia_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pepsirussia-18">[18]</a></sup> (via licensed agreement), <a href="/wiki/Wilson_Sporting_Goods" title="Wilson Sporting Goods">Wilson Sporting Goods</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wilson_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilson-19">[19]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/North_American_Van_Lines" title="North American Van Lines">North American Van Lines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vanlines_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanlines-20">[20]</a></sup></p><p>The divestments concluding in 1997 were followed by multiple large-scale acquisitions, as PepsiCo began to extend its operations beyond soft drinks and snack foods into other lines of foods and beverages. PepsiCo purchased the <a href="/wiki/Orange_juice" title="Orange juice">orange juice</a> company <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Products" title="Tropicana Products">Tropicana Products</a> in 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-tropicana_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tropicana-21">[21]</a></sup> and merged with <a href="/wiki/Quaker_Oats_Company" title="Quaker Oats Company">Quaker Oats Company</a> in 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-quaker2_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quaker2-22">[22]</a></sup> adding with it the <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a> sports drink line and other Quaker Oats brands such as <a href="/wiki/Chewy_Granola_Bars" class="mw-redirect" title="Chewy Granola Bars">Chewy Granola Bars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aunt_Jemima" title="Aunt Jemima">Aunt Jemima</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-quakeroats_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quakeroats-23">[23]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2009, PepsiCo made a $7 billion offer to acquire the two largest bottlers of its products in North America: <a href="/wiki/Pepsi_Bottling_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Pepsi Bottling Group">Pepsi Bottling Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/PepsiAmericas" title="PepsiAmericas">PepsiAmericas</a>. In 2010 this acquisition was completed, resulting in the formation of a new <a href="/wiki/Wholly_owned_subsidiary" class="mw-redirect" title="Wholly owned subsidiary">wholly owned subsidiary</a> of PepsiCo, <i>Pepsi Beverages Company</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-kaplanbottler_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplanbottler-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2011, the company made its largest international acquisition by purchasing a two-thirds (majority) stake in <a href="/wiki/Wimm-Bill-Dann_Foods" title="Wimm-Bill-Dann Foods">Wimm-Bill-Dann Foods</a>, a Russian food company that produces milk, yogurt, fruit juices, and dairy products.<sup id="cite_ref-wimmbfeb_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wimmbfeb-25">[25]</a></sup> When it acquired the remaining 23% stake of Wimm-Bill-Dann Foods in October 2011, PepsiCo became the largest food and beverage company in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-Wimmbd3_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wimmbd3-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wimmbd2_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wimmbd2-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2012, PepsiCo announced a joint venture with the Theo Muller Group which was named Muller Quaker Dairy. This marked PepsiCo's first entry into the dairy space in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The joint venture was dissolved in December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>On May 25, 2018, PepsiCo announced that it would acquire fruit and veggie snack maker <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bare_Foods&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bare Foods (page does not exist)">Bare Foods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> It will also quarter-own <a href="/w/index.php?title=AllMotti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="AllMotti (page does not exist)">allMotti</a> in late November 2018 and it will be PepsiCo's first owned Tech and Computer Service company.
</p><p>On August 20, 2018, PepsiCo announced that it had entered into agreement to acquire <a href="/wiki/SodaStream" title="SodaStream">SodaStream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Pepsi_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Pepsi-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The purchase is expected to close by January 2019 as part of a strategic plan to steer Pepsi toward offering healthier products.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p>In 2019 PepsiCo sued four small farmers in India US$142,000 each for growing a type of potato it says it owns.<sup id="cite_ref-Reu2019_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reu2019-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN2019Farm_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN2019Farm-35">[35]</a></sup> Pepsi said they would end the suit if the farmers grew potatoes for them.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN2019Farm_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN2019Farm-35">[35]</a></sup> A number of Farmers' associations are requesting that the government get involved in the case stating that Pepsi is attempting to intimidate people.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN2019Farm_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN2019Farm-35">[35]</a></sup> After pressure from the public as well as state and national governments, PepsiCo withdrew the lawsuit on May 2, 2019.
</p><p>On October 3, 2019, PepsiCo announced that they will leave <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> after terminating their partnership with local distributor PT Anugerah Indofood Barokah Makmur (AIBM). Both companies stopped production of PepsiCo products on October 10. This has resulted in <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a> chains in the country to switch to Coca-Cola products.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>On December 2, 2019, PepsiCo acquired the snacks brand, BFY Brands, who are going to be folded into the Frito-Lay division.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2020, PepsiCo announced that it had entered into agreement to acquire <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_(drink)" title="Rockstar (drink)">Rockstar Energy</a> for $3.85 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PepsiCo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Competition" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">The Coca-Cola Company</a> has historically been considered PepsiCo's primary competitor in the beverage market,<sup id="cite_ref-pepsicococacola_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pepsicococacola-40">[40]</a></sup> and in December 2005, PepsiCo surpassed The Coca-Cola Company in market value for the first time in 112 years since both companies began to compete. In 2009, The Coca-Cola Company held a higher market share in carbonated <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drink</a> sales within the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-10k_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10k-41">[41]</a></sup> In the same year, PepsiCo maintained a higher share of the U.S. refreshment beverage market, however, reflecting the differences in product lines between the two companies.<sup id="cite_ref-10k_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10k-41">[41]</a></sup> As a result of mergers, acquisitions, and partnerships pursued by PepsiCo in the 1990s and 2000s, its business has shifted to include a broader product base, including foods, snacks, and beverages. The majority of PepsiCo's revenues no longer come from the production and sale of carbonated soft drinks.<sup id="cite_ref-q32010earnings_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-q32010earnings-42">[42]</a></sup> Beverages accounted for less than 50 percent of its total revenue in 2009. In the same year, slightly more than 60 percent of PepsiCo's beverage sales came from its primary non-carbonated brands, namely <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Products" title="Tropicana Products">Tropicana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10k_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10k-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>PepsiCo's <a href="/wiki/Frito-Lay" title="Frito-Lay">Frito-Lay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quaker_Oats" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaker Oats">Quaker Oats</a> brands hold a significant share of the U.S. snack food market, accounting for approximately 39 percent of U.S. snack food sales in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-10k_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10k-41">[41]</a></sup> One of PepsiCo's primary competitors in the snack food market overall is <a href="/wiki/Kraft_Foods" title="Kraft Foods">Kraft Foods</a>, which in the same year held 11 percent of the U.S. snack market share.<sup id="cite_ref-10k_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10k-41">[41]</a></sup>
Other competitors for soda are <a href="/wiki/RC_Cola" title="RC Cola">RC Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cola_Turka" title="Cola Turka">Cola Turka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kola_Real" title="Kola Real">Kola Real</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inca_Kola" title="Inca Kola">Inca Kola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zamzam_Cola" class="mw-redirect" title="Zamzam Cola">Zamzam Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mecca-Cola" title="Mecca-Cola">Mecca-Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Cola" title="Virgin Cola">Virgin Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qibla_Cola" title="Qibla Cola">Qibla Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evoca_Cola" title="Evoca Cola">Evoca Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsica_Cola" title="Corsica Cola">Corsica Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breizh_Cola" title="Breizh Cola">Breizh Cola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Afri_Cola" class="mw-redirect" title="Afri Cola">Afri Cola</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PepsiCo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Soviet Union" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1959, the <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a> held an exhibition of Soviet technology and culture in New York. The United States reciprocated with an exhibition in <a href="/wiki/Sokolniki_Park" title="Sokolniki Park">Sokolniki Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, which led to the famous <a href="/wiki/Kitchen_debate" class="mw-redirect" title="Kitchen debate">kitchen debate</a>. One of the American products exhibited was Pepsi Cola. After obtaining a photo of U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> and Soviet Premier <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> sipping Pepsi, Pepsico executive Donald Kendall was able to capture the attention of the Soviet people and, in 1972, negotiate a cola monopoly in the USSR. Due to Soviet restrictions on transporting rubles abroad, PepsiCo struck a <a href="/wiki/Barter" title="Barter">barter deal</a> whereby <a href="/wiki/Stolichnaya" title="Stolichnaya">Stolichnaya</a> vodka would be exchanged for Pepsi syrup. This deal lasted until 1990, when the USSR and PepsiCo re-negotiated a $3 billion deal to exchange syrup for vodka and a small fleet of Soviet warships including 17 submarines, a frigate, a cruiser and a destroyer.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PepsiCo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Finances" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>For the fiscal year 2017, PepsiCo reported earnings of US$4.857 billion, with an annual revenue of US$62.525 billion, an increase of 1.2% over the previous fiscal cycle. PepsiCo's shares traded at over $109 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$155.9 billion in September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> PepsiCo ranked No. 45 on the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
